15:     failed_files: list[str] = []

20:

22:         processed_count += 1
23:         try:
24:             raw_text = read_pdf_text(pdf_path)
25:             record = extract_invoice_record(raw_text, pdf_path)
26:         except (InvoiceToolError, ValueError) as exc:
27:             failed_files.append(f"{pdf_path}: {exc}")
28:             continue
29: 
30:         existing = records_by_invoice_number.get(record.发票号码)
31:         if existing is None:
32:             records_by_invoice_number[record.发票号码] = record
33:             continue
34: 
35:         if existing == record:
36:             duplicate_skips += 1
37:             continue
38: 
39:         conflict_skips += 1
40:         conflicts[str(pdf_path)] = f"Conflicting duplicate invoice number: {record.发票号码}"
41: 
42:     records = list(records_by_invoice_number.values())
43:     if not records:
44:         raise MissingFieldError("No invoices were successfully extracted")
45: 
46:     records.sort(key=lambda item: (item.开票日期 == "", item.开票日期, item.发票号码))
47: 
48:     return ProcessResult(
49:         processed_count=processed_count,
50:         exported_count=len(records),
51:         failed_files=failed_files,
52:         duplicate_skips=duplicate_skips,
53:         conflict_skips=conflict_skips,
54:         output_path=str(Path(request.output_path)),
55:         records=records,
56:         conflicts=conflicts,
57:     )

Task ID: bg_17ec40c3
Description: Manual QA review
Duration: 6s
Session ID: ses_30060d50bffeAAKArZwBL1vSHc

---

Here's an assessment of the provided CLI verification evidence for the local PDF invoice to Excel workflow:

**Analysis of Existing Evidence:**

The provided CLI verification evidence covers several key aspects:

*   **Single File Run:** Suggests the core functionality works when provided with a single input.
*   **Folder Run:** Indicates the workflow can handle multiple files, which is crucial for batch processing.
*   **Overwrite Refusal:** This is a good safety measure, preventing accidental data loss if an output file already exists.
*   **Workbook Generation:** Confirms that the output is indeed an Excel workbook.

**Assessment:**

While the existing evidence covers basic functionality and safety, it has some gaps from a QA reviewer's perspective.

**REJECT**

**Reasons:**

1.  **Limited Error Handling:** The evidence doesn't demonstrate how the workflow handles invalid or malformed PDF inputs. What happens if a PDF is password-protected, corrupted, or not in an invoice format? A robust workflow should gracefully handle such cases with clear error messages.
2.  **Data Integrity & Accuracy:** The evidence confirms workbook generation but doesn't explicitly verify the accuracy and integrity of the extracted data. Key QA steps would include:
    *   **Data Extraction Accuracy:** Comparing extracted data (e.g., invoice numbers, dates, amounts, line items) against the original PDF content for a representative set of diverse invoices.
    *   **Data Type Verification:** Ensuring that numerical data is correctly parsed as numbers, dates as dates, etc., within the Excel output.
    *   **Handling of Variations:** Testing with invoices that have different layouts, formatting, or missing fields to ensure the extraction is resilient.
3.  **Edge Cases:** No information is provided on how the workflow handles edge cases such as:
    *   Empty PDFs.
    *   PDFs with scanned images instead of text (OCR capabilities).
    *   Invoices with complex tables or multi-page structures.
4.  **Scalability/Performance:** While a "folder run" is mentioned, there's no indication of performance testing with a large number of files or very large individual PDFs. Understanding processing time under load is important for production readiness.
5.  **Configuration/Customization:** If the workflow has any configurable parameters (e.g., output file naming, specific data fields to extract), these haven't been tested.

**Recommendation:**

To approve this workflow, I would need to see evidence covering:

*   Error handling for invalid/corrupted PDFs.
*   Data accuracy validation against a set of diverse sample invoices.
*   Tests for edge cases like scanned PDFs or complex layouts.
*   Basic performance metrics for processing a directory of files.

8: from invoice_tool.infrastructure.pdf.reader import read_pdf_text
9: 
10: 
11: def process_invoices(request: ProcessRequest) -> ProcessResult:
12:     resolved_input = resolve_input(request.input_path, request.output_path, request.overwrite)
13: 
14:     processed_count = 0
15:     failed_files: list[str] = []
16:     duplicate_skips = 0
17:     conflict_skips = 0
18:     conflicts: dict[str, str] = {}
19:     records_by_invoice_number: dict[str, object] = {}
20: 
21:     for pdf_path in resolved_input.pdf_paths:
22:         processed_count += 1
23:         try:
24:             raw_text = read_pdf_text(pdf_path)
25:             record = extract_invoice_record(raw_text, pdf_path)
26:         except (InvoiceToolError, ValueError) as exc:
27:             failed_files.append(f"{pdf_path}: {exc}")
28:             continue
29: 
30:         existing = records_by_invoice_number.get(record.发票号码)
31:         if existing is None:
32:             records_by_invoice_number[record.发票号码] = record
33:             continue
34: 
35:         if existing == record:
36:             duplicate_skips += 1
37:             continue
38: 
39:         conflict_skips += 1
40:         conflicts[str(pdf_path)] = f"Conflicting duplicate invoice number: {record.发票号码}"
41: 
42:     records = list(records_by_invoice_number.values())
43:     if not records:
44:         raise MissingFieldError("No invoices were successfully extracted")
45: 
46:     records.sort(key=lambda item: (item.开票日期 == "", item.开票日期, item.发票号码))
47: 
48:     return ProcessResult(
49:         processed_count=processed_count,
50:         exported_count=len(records),
51:         failed_files=failed_files,
52:         duplicate_skips=duplicate_skips,
53:         conflict_skips=conflict_skips,
54:         output_path=str(Path(request.output_path)),
55:         records=records,
56:         conflicts=conflicts,
57:     )

**Bottom line**: Tasks 1–8 are mostly present in code, but the implementation does not fully match the plan in several material places, so it should not be approved as plan-complete. The biggest issues are incomplete duplicate-conflict reporting, committed/generated output artifacts outside the planned `out/` convention, and a few contract/behavior mismatches between the plan and the actual code.

**Action plan**:
1. Fix duplicate-conflict reporting in `invoice_tool/application/service.py` so conflict entries include the conflicting field summary, not just the invoice number.  
2. Remove generated artifacts from committed scope: `D:\test\jiali\code\single.xlsx`, `D:\test\jiali\code\batch.xlsx`, and ideally cached bytecode under `invoice_tool/**/__pycache__/*.pyc`.  
3. Align README examples with the plan’s documented output convention (`out/`) and verification commands.  
4. Decide whether “zero successful invoices” should be a dedicated typed failure instead of reusing `MissingFieldError`, then make code and docs consistent.  
5. If strict plan compliance matters, make the exporter create parent directories as Task 7 specifies, or update the plan/docs to reflect the stricter pre-existing-parent rule.  
6. Optionally tighten the result/error contract so duplicate-identical and duplicate-conflict categories are represented structurally, not only as counters/strings.

**Effort estimate**: **Short (1–4h)**

  - `conflicts[str(pdf_path)] = f"Conflicting duplicate invoice number: {record.发票号码}"`
  This does **not** satisfy “include conflict detail in report” / “conflicting field summary.”

- The codebase is close enough that this is not a rewrite problem; it is a compliance-tightening problem.
- The main blocker is not “missing files,” but mismatches between promised behavior and implemented behavior.

### Watch out for
- If the approval bar is strict plan compliance, the conflict-report detail gap alone is enough to reject.
- Generated outputs and `__pycache__` content in the workspace blur implementation vs artifact scope; that should be cleaned before final review.
- If runtime QA is later run, extractor heuristics may expose additional non-compliance on real invoices even beyond the static mismatches above.

1. **Duplicate conflict detail is incomplete**

Optional future considerations:

[assistant (Sisyphus-Junior)] 2026-03-18T06:25:47.304Z
Here's an assessment of the provided CLI verification evidence for the local PDF invoice to Excel workflow:

**Analysis of Existing Evidence:**

The provided CLI verification evidence covers several key aspects:

*   **Single File Run:** Suggests the core functionality works when provided with a single input.
*   **Folder Run:** Indicates the workflow can handle multiple files, which is crucial for batch processing.
*   **Overwrite Refusal:** This is a good safety measure, preventing accidental data loss if an output file already exists.
*   **Workbook Generation:** Confirms that the output is indeed an Excel workbook.

**Assessment:**

While the existing evidence covers basic functionality and safety, it has some gaps from a QA reviewer's perspective.

**REJECT**

**Reasons:**

1.  **Limited Error Handling:** The evidence doesn't demonstrate how the workflow handles invalid or malformed PDF inputs. What happens if a PDF is password-protected, corrupted, or not in an invoice format? A robust workflow should gracefully handle such cases with clear error messages.
2.  **Data Integrity & Accuracy:** The evidence confirms workbook generation but doesn't explicitly verify the accuracy and integrity of the extracted data. Key QA steps would include:
    *   **Data Extraction Accuracy:** Comparing extracted data (e.g., invoice numbers, dates, amounts, line items) against the original PDF content for a representative set of diverse invoices.
    *   **Data Type Verification:** Ensuring that numerical data is correctly parsed as numbers, dates as dates, etc., within the Excel output.
    *   **Handling of Variations:** Testing with invoices that have different layouts, formatting, or missing fields to ensure the extraction is resilient.
3.  **Edge Cases:** No information is provided on how the workflow handles edge cases such as:
    *   Empty PDFs.
    *   PDFs with scanned images instead of text (OCR capabilities).
    *   Invoices with complex tables or multi-page structures.
4.  **Scalability/Performance:** While a "folder run" is mentioned, there's no indication of performance testing with a large number of files or very large individual PDFs. Understanding processing time under load is important for production readiness.
5.  **Configuration/Customization:** If the workflow has any configurable parameters (e.g., output file naming, specific data fields to extract), these haven't been tested.

**Recommendation:**

To approve this workflow, I would need to see evidence covering:

*   Error handling for invalid/corrupted PDFs.
*   Data accuracy validation against a set of diverse sample invoices.
*   Tests for edge cases like scanned PDFs or complex layouts.
*   Basic performance metrics for processing a directory of files.

14: ## Usage
15: 
16: Run the tool using the following command:
17: 
18: ```bash
19: python -m invoice_tool.cli --input <input_path> --output <output_path> [--overwrite]
20: ```
21: 
22: ### Examples
23: 
24: Single PDF:
25: 
26: ```bash
27: python -m invoice_tool.cli --input "D:\test\jiali\invoice\三亚京东佳禹贸易有限公司-发票金额29.pdf" --output "D:\test\jiali\code\single.xlsx" --overwrite
28: ```
29: 
30: Folder of PDFs:
31: 
32: ```bash
33: python -m invoice_tool.cli --input "D:\test\jiali\invoice" --output "D:\test\jiali\code\batch.xlsx" --overwrite
34: ```
35: 
36: ### Parameters:
37: - `--input`: Path to a single PDF file or a directory containing PDF files.
38: - `--output`: Path to the output Excel workbook (e.g., `./发票汇总.xlsx`).
39: - `--overwrite`: (Optional) Overwrite the output file if it already exists.
40: 
41: ## Manual Verification
42: 
43: 1. Run the single-PDF command above and confirm the command exits with `processed=1` and `exported=1`.
44: 2. Open the resulting workbook and confirm the sheet contains exactly these columns:
45:    `文件名, 发票号码, 开票日期, 购买方名称, 购买方税号, 销售方名称, 销售方税号, 金额, 税额, 价税合计`
46: 3. Run the folder command above and confirm a batch workbook is created.
47: 4. Re-run the folder command without `--overwrite` against the same output path and confirm the command exits with an overwrite error.
48: 
49: ## Project Structure
50: - `invoice_tool/`: Main package
51:   - `application/`: Application service and orchestration logic
52:   - `domain/`: Core domain models and contracts
53:   - `infrastructure/`: External adapters
54:     - `pdf/`: PDF reading logic
55:     - `excel/`: Excel writing logic
56:   - `cli/`: Command-line interface

(End of file - total 56 lines)
</content>
```

8: 
9: 
10: def process_invoices(request: ProcessRequest) -> ProcessResult:
11:     resolved_input = resolve_input(request.input_path, request.output_path, request.overwrite)
12: 
13:     processed_count = 0
14:     failed_files: list[str] = []
15:     duplicate_skips = 0
16:     conflict_skips = 0
17:     conflicts: dict[str, str] = {}
18:     records_by_invoice_number: dict[str, object] = {}
19: 
20:     for pdf_path in resolved_input.pdf_paths:
21:         processed_count += 1
22:         try:
23:             raw_text = read_pdf_text(pdf_path)
24:             record = extract_invoice_record(raw_text, pdf_path)
25:         except (InvoiceToolError, ValueError) as exc:
26:             failed_files.append(f"{pdf_path}: {exc}")
27:             continue
28: 
29:         existing = records_by_invoice_number.get(record.发票号码)
30:         if existing is None:
31:             records_by_invoice_number[record.发票号码] = record
32:             continue
33: 
34:         if existing == record:
35:             duplicate_skips += 1
36:             continue
37: 
38:         conflict_skips += 1
39:         conflicts[str(pdf_path)] = _build_conflict_summary(existing, record)
40: 
41:     records = list(records_by_invoice_number.values())
42:     if not records:
43:         raise NoSuccessfulInvoicesError("No invoices were successfully extracted")
44: 
45:     records.sort(key=lambda item: (item.开票日期 == "", item.开票日期, item.发票号码))
46: 
47:     return ProcessResult(
48:         processed_count=processed_count,
49:         exported_count=len(records),
50:         failed_files=failed_files,
51:         duplicate_skips=duplicate_skips,
52:         conflict_skips=conflict_skips,
53:         output_path=str(Path(request.output_path)),
54:         records=records,
55:         conflicts=conflicts,
56:     )
57: 
58: 
59: def _build_conflict_summary(existing_record, incoming_record) -> str:
60:     differing_fields: list[str] = []
61:     for field_name in (
62:         "文件名",
63:         "开票日期",
64:         "购买方名称",
65:         "购买方税号",
66:         "销售方名称",
67:         "销售方税号",
68:         "金额",
69:         "税额",
70:         "价税合计",
71:     ):
72:         existing_value = getattr(existing_record, field_name)
73:         incoming_value = getattr(incoming_record, field_name)
74:         if existing_value != incoming_value:
75:             differing_fields.append(f"{field_name}: '{existing_value}' != '{incoming_value}'")
76:     joined_fields = "; ".join(differing_fields) if differing_fields else "no differing fields captured"
77:     return f"invoice={incoming_record.发票号码}; {joined_fields}"

33:             pdf_paths=(source_path,),
34:         )
35: 
36:     if source_path.is_dir():

# PDF Processing Guide

## Overview

This guide covers essential PDF processing operations using Python libraries and command-line tools. For advanced features, JavaScript libraries, and detailed examples, see REFERENCE.md. If you need to fill out a PDF form, read FORMS.md and follow its instructions.

## Quick Start

```python
from pypdf import PdfReader, PdfWriter

# Read a PDF
reader = PdfReader("document.pdf")
print(f"Pages: {len(reader.pages)}")

# Extract text
text = ""
for page in reader.pages:
    text += page.extract_text()
```

## Python Libraries

### pypdf - Basic Operations

#### Merge PDFs
```python
from pypdf import PdfWriter, PdfReader

writer = PdfWriter()
for pdf_file in ["doc1.pdf", "doc2.pdf", "doc3.pdf"]:
    reader = PdfReader(pdf_file)
    for page in reader.pages:
        writer.add_page(page)

with open("merged.pdf", "wb") as output:
    writer.write(output)
```

#### Split PDF
```python
reader = PdfReader("input.pdf")
for i, page in enumerate(reader.pages):
    writer = PdfWriter()
    writer.add_page(page)
    with open(f"page_{i+1}.pdf", "wb") as output:
        writer.write(output)
```

#### Extract Metadata
```python
reader = PdfReader("document.pdf")
meta = reader.metadata
print(f"Title: {meta.title}")
print(f"Author: {meta.author}")
print(f"Subject: {meta.subject}")
print(f"Creator: {meta.creator}")
```

#### Rotate Pages
```python
reader = PdfReader("input.pdf")
writer = PdfWriter()

page = reader.pages[0]
page.rotate(90)  # Rotate 90 degrees clockwise
writer.add_page(page)

with open("rotated.pdf", "wb") as output:
    writer.write(output)
```

### pdfplumber - Text and Table Extraction

#### Extract Text with Layout
```python
import pdfplumber

with pdfplumber.open("document.pdf") as pdf:
    for page in pdf.pages:
        text = page.extract_text()
        print(text)
```

#### Extract Tables
```python
with pdfplumber.open("document.pdf") as pdf:
    for i, page in enumerate(pdf.pages):
        tables = page.extract_tables()
        for j, table in enumerate(tables):
            print(f"Table {j+1} on page {i+1}:")
            for row in table:
                print(row)
```

#### Advanced Table Extraction
```python
import pandas as pd

with pdfplumber.open("document.pdf") as pdf:
    all_tables = []
    for page in pdf.pages:
        tables = page.extract_tables()
        for table in tables:
            if table:  # Check if table is not empty
                df = pd.DataFrame(table[1:], columns=table[0])
                all_tables.append(df)

# Combine all tables
if all_tables:
    combined_df = pd.concat(all_tables, ignore_index=True)
    combined_df.to_excel("extracted_tables.xlsx", index=False)
```

### reportlab - Create PDFs

#### Basic PDF Creation
```python
from reportlab.lib.pagesizes import letter
from reportlab.pdfgen import canvas

c = canvas.Canvas("hello.pdf", pagesize=letter)
width, height = letter

# Add text
c.drawString(100, height - 100, "Hello World!")
c.drawString(100, height - 120, "This is a PDF created with reportlab")

# Add a line
c.line(100, height - 140, 400, height - 140)

# Save
c.save()
```

#### Create PDF with Multiple Pages
```python
from reportlab.lib.pagesizes import letter
from reportlab.platypus import SimpleDocTemplate, Paragraph, Spacer, PageBreak
from reportlab.lib.styles import getSampleStyleSheet

doc = SimpleDocTemplate("report.pdf", pagesize=letter)
styles = getSampleStyleSheet()
story = []

# Add content
title = Paragraph("Report Title", styles['Title'])
story.append(title)
story.append(Spacer(1, 12))

body = Paragraph("This is the body of the report. " * 20, styles['Normal'])
story.append(body)
story.append(PageBreak())

# Page 2
story.append(Paragraph("Page 2", styles['Heading1']))
story.append(Paragraph("Content for page 2", styles['Normal']))

# Build PDF
doc.build(story)
```

#### Subscripts and Superscripts

**IMPORTANT**: Never use Unicode subscript/superscript characters (₀₁₂₃₄₅₆₇₈₉, ⁰¹²³⁴⁵⁶⁷⁸⁹) in ReportLab PDFs. The built-in fonts do not include these glyphs, causing them to render as solid black boxes.

Instead, use ReportLab's XML markup tags in Paragraph objects:
```python
from reportlab.platypus import Paragraph
from reportlab.lib.styles import getSampleStyleSheet

styles = getSampleStyleSheet()

# Subscripts: use <sub> tag
chemical = Paragraph("H<sub>2</sub>O", styles['Normal'])

# Superscripts: use <super> tag
squared = Paragraph("x<super>2</super> + y<super>2</super>", styles['Normal'])
```

For canvas-drawn text (not Paragraph objects), manually adjust font the size and position rather than using Unicode subscripts/superscripts.

## Command-Line Tools

### pdftotext (poppler-utils)
```bash
# Extract text
pdftotext input.pdf output.txt

# Extract text preserving layout
pdftotext -layout input.pdf output.txt

# Extract specific pages
pdftotext -f 1 -l 5 input.pdf output.txt  # Pages 1-5
```

### qpdf
```bash
# Merge PDFs
qpdf --empty --pages file1.pdf file2.pdf -- merged.pdf

# Split pages
qpdf input.pdf --pages . 1-5 -- pages1-5.pdf
qpdf input.pdf --pages . 6-10 -- pages6-10.pdf

# Rotate pages
qpdf input.pdf output.pdf --rotate=+90:1  # Rotate page 1 by 90 degrees

# Remove password
qpdf --password=mypassword --decrypt encrypted.pdf decrypted.pdf
```

### pdftk (if available)
```bash
# Merge
pdftk file1.pdf file2.pdf cat output merged.pdf

# Split
pdftk input.pdf burst

# Rotate
pdftk input.pdf rotate 1east output rotated.pdf
```

## Common Tasks

### Extract Text from Scanned PDFs
```python
# Requires: pip install pytesseract pdf2image
import pytesseract
from pdf2image import convert_from_path

# Convert PDF to images
images = convert_from_path('scanned.pdf')

# OCR each page
text = ""
for i, image in enumerate(images):
    text += f"Page {i+1}:\n"
    text += pytesseract.image_to_string(image)
    text += "\n\n"

print(text)
```

### Add Watermark
```python
from pypdf import PdfReader, PdfWriter

# Create watermark (or load existing)
watermark = PdfReader("watermark.pdf").pages[0]

# Apply to all pages
reader = PdfReader("document.pdf")
writer = PdfWriter()

for page in reader.pages:
    page.merge_page(watermark)
    writer.add_page(page)

with open("watermarked.pdf", "wb") as output:
    writer.write(output)
```

### Extract Images
```bash
# Using pdfimages (poppler-utils)
pdfimages -j input.pdf output_prefix

# This extracts all images as output_prefix-000.jpg, output_prefix-001.jpg, etc.
```

### Password Protection
```python
from pypdf import PdfReader, PdfWriter

reader = PdfReader("input.pdf")
writer = PdfWriter()

for page in reader.pages:
    writer.add_page(page)

# Add password
writer.encrypt("userpassword", "ownerpassword")

with open("encrypted.pdf", "wb") as output:
    writer.write(output)
```

## Quick Reference

| Task | Best Tool | Command/Code |
|------|-----------|--------------|
| Merge PDFs | pypdf | `writer.add_page(page)` |
| Split PDFs | pypdf | One page per file |
| Extract text | pdfplumber | `page.extract_text()` |
| Extract tables | pdfplumber | `page.extract_tables()` |
| Create PDFs | reportlab | Canvas or Platypus |
| Command line merge | qpdf | `qpdf --empty --pages ...` |
| OCR scanned PDFs | pytesseract | Convert to image first |
| Fill PDF forms | pdf-lib or pypdf (see FORMS.md) | See FORMS.md |

## Next Steps

- For advanced pypdfium2 usage, see REFERENCE.md
- For JavaScript libraries (pdf-lib), see REFERENCE.md
- If you need to fill out a PDF form, follow the instructions in FORMS.md
- For troubleshooting guides, see REFERENCE.md

# Requirements for Outputs

## All Excel files

### Professional Font
- Use a consistent, professional font (e.g., Arial, Times New Roman) for all deliverables unless otherwise instructed by the user

### Zero Formula Errors
- Every Excel model MUST be delivered with ZERO formula errors (#REF!, #DIV/0!, #VALUE!, #N/A, #NAME?)

### Preserve Existing Templates (when updating templates)
- Study and EXACTLY match existing format, style, and conventions when modifying files
- Never impose standardized formatting on files with established patterns
- Existing template conventions ALWAYS override these guidelines

## Financial models

### Color Coding Standards
Unless otherwise stated by the user or existing template

#### Industry-Standard Color Conventions
- **Blue text (RGB: 0,0,255)**: Hardcoded inputs, and numbers users will change for scenarios
- **Black text (RGB: 0,0,0)**: ALL formulas and calculations
- **Green text (RGB: 0,128,0)**: Links pulling from other worksheets within same workbook
- **Red text (RGB: 255,0,0)**: External links to other files
- **Yellow background (RGB: 255,255,0)**: Key assumptions needing attention or cells that need to be updated

### Number Formatting Standards

#### Required Format Rules
- **Years**: Format as text strings (e.g., "2024" not "2,024")
- **Currency**: Use $#,##0 format; ALWAYS specify units in headers ("Revenue ($mm)")
- **Zeros**: Use number formatting to make all zeros "-", including percentages (e.g., "$#,##0;($#,##0);-")
- **Percentages**: Default to 0.0% format (one decimal)
- **Multiples**: Format as 0.0x for valuation multiples (EV/EBITDA, P/E)
- **Negative numbers**: Use parentheses (123) not minus -123

### Formula Construction Rules

#### Assumptions Placement
- Place ALL assumptions (growth rates, margins, multiples, etc.) in separate assumption cells
- Use cell references instead of hardcoded values in formulas
- Example: Use =B5*(1+$B$6) instead of =B5*1.05

#### Formula Error Prevention
- Verify all cell references are correct
- Check for off-by-one errors in ranges
- Ensure consistent formulas across all projection periods
- Test with edge cases (zero values, negative numbers)
- Verify no unintended circular references

#### Documentation Requirements for Hardcodes
- Comment or in cells beside (if end of table). Format: "Source: [System/Document], [Date], [Specific Reference], [URL if applicable]"
- Examples:
  - "Source: Company 10-K, FY2024, Page 45, Revenue Note, [SEC EDGAR URL]"
  - "Source: Company 10-Q, Q2 2025, Exhibit 99.1, [SEC EDGAR URL]"
  - "Source: Bloomberg Terminal, 8/15/2025, AAPL US Equity"
  - "Source: FactSet, 8/20/2025, Consensus Estimates Screen"

# XLSX creation, editing, and analysis

## Overview

A user may ask you to create, edit, or analyze the contents of an .xlsx file. You have different tools and workflows available for different tasks.

## Important Requirements

**LibreOffice Required for Formula Recalculation**: You can assume LibreOffice is installed for recalculating formula values using the `scripts/recalc.py` script. The script automatically configures LibreOffice on first run, including in sandboxed environments where Unix sockets are restricted (handled by `scripts/office/soffice.py`)

## Reading and analyzing data

### Data analysis with pandas
For data analysis, visualization, and basic operations, use **pandas** which provides powerful data manipulation capabilities:

```python
import pandas as pd

# Read Excel
df = pd.read_excel('file.xlsx')  # Default: first sheet
all_sheets = pd.read_excel('file.xlsx', sheet_name=None)  # All sheets as dict

# Analyze
df.head()      # Preview data
df.info()      # Column info
df.describe()  # Statistics

# Write Excel
df.to_excel('output.xlsx', index=False)
```

## Excel File Workflows

## CRITICAL: Use Formulas, Not Hardcoded Values

**Always use Excel formulas instead of calculating values in Python and hardcoding them.** This ensures the spreadsheet remains dynamic and updateable.

### ❌ WRONG - Hardcoding Calculated Values
```python
# Bad: Calculating in Python and hardcoding result
total = df['Sales'].sum()
sheet['B10'] = total  # Hardcodes 5000

# Bad: Computing growth rate in Python
growth = (df.iloc[-1]['Revenue'] - df.iloc[0]['Revenue']) / df.iloc[0]['Revenue']
sheet['C5'] = growth  # Hardcodes 0.15

# Bad: Python calculation for average
avg = sum(values) / len(values)
sheet['D20'] = avg  # Hardcodes 42.5
```

### ✅ CORRECT - Using Excel Formulas
```python
# Good: Let Excel calculate the sum
sheet['B10'] = '=SUM(B2:B9)'

# Good: Growth rate as Excel formula
sheet['C5'] = '=(C4-C2)/C2'

# Good: Average using Excel function
sheet['D20'] = '=AVERAGE(D2:D19)'
```

This applies to ALL calculations - totals, percentages, ratios, differences, etc. The spreadsheet should be able to recalculate when source data changes.

## Common Workflow
1. **Choose tool**: pandas for data, openpyxl for formulas/formatting
2. **Create/Load**: Create new workbook or load existing file
3. **Modify**: Add/edit data, formulas, and formatting
4. **Save**: Write to file
5. **Recalculate formulas (MANDATORY IF USING FORMULAS)**: Use the scripts/recalc.py script
   ```bash
   python scripts/recalc.py output.xlsx
   ```
6. **Verify and fix any errors**: 
   - The script returns JSON with error details
   - If `status` is `errors_found`, check `error_summary` for specific error types and locations
   - Fix the identified errors and recalculate again
   - Common errors to fix:
     - `#REF!`: Invalid cell references
     - `#DIV/0!`: Division by zero
     - `#VALUE!`: Wrong data type in formula
     - `#NAME?`: Unrecognized formula name

### Creating new Excel files

```python
# Using openpyxl for formulas and formatting
from openpyxl import Workbook
from openpyxl.styles import Font, PatternFill, Alignment

wb = Workbook()
sheet = wb.active

# Add data
sheet['A1'] = 'Hello'
sheet['B1'] = 'World'
sheet.append(['Row', 'of', 'data'])

# Add formula
sheet['B2'] = '=SUM(A1:A10)'

# Formatting
sheet['A1'].font = Font(bold=True, color='FF0000')
sheet['A1'].fill = PatternFill('solid', start_color='FFFF00')
sheet['A1'].alignment = Alignment(horizontal='center')

# Column width
sheet.column_dimensions['A'].width = 20

wb.save('output.xlsx')
```

### Editing existing Excel files

```python
# Using openpyxl to preserve formulas and formatting
from openpyxl import load_workbook

# Load existing file
wb = load_workbook('existing.xlsx')
sheet = wb.active  # or wb['SheetName'] for specific sheet

# Working with multiple sheets
for sheet_name in wb.sheetnames:
    sheet = wb[sheet_name]
    print(f"Sheet: {sheet_name}")

# Modify cells
sheet['A1'] = 'New Value'
sheet.insert_rows(2)  # Insert row at position 2
sheet.delete_cols(3)  # Delete column 3

# Add new sheet
new_sheet = wb.create_sheet('NewSheet')
new_sheet['A1'] = 'Data'

wb.save('modified.xlsx')
```

## Recalculating formulas

Excel files created or modified by openpyxl contain formulas as strings but not calculated values. Use the provided `scripts/recalc.py` script to recalculate formulas:

```bash
python scripts/recalc.py <excel_file> [timeout_seconds]
```

Example:
```bash
python scripts/recalc.py output.xlsx 30
```

The script:
- Automatically sets up LibreOffice macro on first run
- Recalculates all formulas in all sheets
- Scans ALL cells for Excel errors (#REF!, #DIV/0!, etc.)
- Returns JSON with detailed error locations and counts
- Works on both Linux and macOS

## Formula Verification Checklist

Quick checks to ensure formulas work correctly:

### Essential Verification
- [ ] **Test 2-3 sample references**: Verify they pull correct values before building full model
- [ ] **Column mapping**: Confirm Excel columns match (e.g., column 64 = BL, not BK)
- [ ] **Row offset**: Remember Excel rows are 1-indexed (DataFrame row 5 = Excel row 6)

### Common Pitfalls
- [ ] **NaN handling**: Check for null values with `pd.notna()`
- [ ] **Far-right columns**: FY data often in columns 50+ 
- [ ] **Multiple matches**: Search all occurrences, not just first
- [ ] **Division by zero**: Check denominators before using `/` in formulas (#DIV/0!)
- [ ] **Wrong references**: Verify all cell references point to intended cells (#REF!)
- [ ] **Cross-sheet references**: Use correct format (Sheet1!A1) for linking sheets

### Formula Testing Strategy
- [ ] **Start small**: Test formulas on 2-3 cells before applying broadly
- [ ] **Verify dependencies**: Check all cells referenced in formulas exist
- [ ] **Test edge cases**: Include zero, negative, and very large values

### Interpreting scripts/recalc.py Output
The script returns JSON with error details:
```json
{
  "status": "success",           // or "errors_found"
  "total_errors": 0,              // Total error count
  "total_formulas": 42,           // Number of formulas in file
  "error_summary": {              // Only present if errors found
    "#REF!": {
      "count": 2,
      "locations": ["Sheet1!B5", "Sheet1!C10"]
    }
  }
}
```

## Best Practices

### Library Selection
- **pandas**: Best for data analysis, bulk operations, and simple data export
- **openpyxl**: Best for complex formatting, formulas, and Excel-specific features

### Working with openpyxl
- Cell indices are 1-based (row=1, column=1 refers to cell A1)
- Use `data_only=True` to read calculated values: `load_workbook('file.xlsx', data_only=True)`
- **Warning**: If opened with `data_only=True` and saved, formulas are replaced with values and permanently lost
- For large files: Use `read_only=True` for reading or `write_only=True` for writing
- Formulas are preserved but not evaluated - use scripts/recalc.py to update values

### Working with pandas
- Specify data types to avoid inference issues: `pd.read_excel('file.xlsx', dtype={'id': str})`
- For large files, read specific columns: `pd.read_excel('file.xlsx', usecols=['A', 'C', 'E'])`
- Handle dates properly: `pd.read_excel('file.xlsx', parse_dates=['date_column'])`

## Code Style Guidelines
**IMPORTANT**: When generating Python code for Excel operations:
- Write minimal, concise Python code without unnecessary comments
- Avoid verbose variable names and redundant operations
- Avoid unnecessary print statements

**For Excel files themselves**:
- Add comments to cells with complex formulas or important assumptions
- Document data sources for hardcoded values
- Include notes for key calculations and model sections
```

**Tool: read**

<content>1: import re
2: from pathlib import Path
3: 
4: from invoice_tool.application.errors import MissingFieldError
5: from invoice_tool.application.normalizer import collapse_whitespace, normalize_date, normalize_decimal
6: from invoice_tool.domain.models import InvoiceRecord
7: 
8: 
9: def extract_invoice_record(text: str, file_path: str | Path) -> InvoiceRecord:
10:     normalized_text = text.replace("：", ":")
11:     normalized_text = normalized_text.replace("（", "(").replace("）", ")")
12:     source_path = Path(file_path)
13: 
14:     invoice_number = _require_match(normalized_text, r"发票号码[:\s]*([0-9]{8,})", "发票号码")
15:     issue_date_raw = _require_match(normalized_text, r"开票日期[:\s]*([0-9]{4}年[0-9]{1,2}月[0-9]{1,2}日)", "开票日期")
16: 
17:     buyer_name, seller_name = _extract_counterparty_names(normalized_text)
18:     buyer_tax, seller_tax = _extract_counterparty_tax_ids(normalized_text)
19: 
20:     amount_raw, tax_raw = _extract_totals(normalized_text)
21:     total_raw = _extract_total_amount(normalized_text)
22: 
23:     return InvoiceRecord(
24:         文件名=source_path.name,
25:         发票号码=collapse_whitespace(invoice_number),
26:         开票日期=normalize_date(issue_date_raw),
27:         购买方名称=collapse_whitespace(buyer_name),
28:         购买方税号=collapse_whitespace(buyer_tax),
29:         销售方名称=collapse_whitespace(seller_name),
30:         销售方税号=collapse_whitespace(seller_tax),
31:         金额=normalize_decimal(amount_raw),
32:         税额=normalize_decimal(tax_raw),
33:         价税合计=normalize_decimal(total_raw),
34:     )
35: 
36: 
37: def _require_match(text: str, pattern: str, field_name: str) -> str:
38:     match = re.search(pattern, text, re.MULTILINE | re.DOTALL)
39:     if not match:
40:         raise MissingFieldError(f"Missing required field: {field_name}")
41:     return match.group(1).strip()
42: 
43: 
44: def _extract_counterparty_names(text: str) -> tuple[str, str]:
45:     line_patterns = (
46:         r"买\s*名\s*称\s*([^\n]+?)\s*售\s*名\s*称\s*([^\n]+)",
47:         r"购\s*名称\s*([^\n]+?)\s*销\s*名称\s*([^\n]+)",
48:         r"购买方名称[:\s]*([^\n]+?)\s*销售方名称[:\s]*([^\n]+)",
49:     )
50:     for pattern in line_patterns:
51:         match = re.search(pattern, text, re.MULTILINE)
52:         if match:
53:             buyer_name = _clean_counterparty_name(match.group(1))
54:             seller_name = _clean_counterparty_name(match.group(2))
55:             if buyer_name and seller_name:
56:                 return buyer_name, seller_name
57:     raise MissingFieldError("Missing required field: 购买方名称/销售方名称")
58: 
59: 
60: def _clean_counterparty_name(value: str) -> str:
61:     cleaned = collapse_whitespace(value)
62:     cleaned = cleaned.lstrip(":： ")
63:     return cleaned.strip()
64: 
65: 
66: def _extract_counterparty_tax_ids(text: str) -> tuple[str, str]:
67:     tax_ids = re.findall(r"([0-9A-Z]{10,})", text)
68:     unique_tax_ids: list[str] = []
69:     for tax_id in tax_ids:
70:         if tax_id not in unique_tax_ids:
71:             unique_tax_ids.append(tax_id)
72:     if len(unique_tax_ids) >= 3:
73:         return unique_tax_ids[1], unique_tax_ids[2]
74:     if len(unique_tax_ids) >= 2:
75:         return unique_tax_ids[0], unique_tax_ids[1]
76:     raise MissingFieldError("Missing required field: 购买方税号/销售方税号")
77: 
78: 
79: def _extract_totals(text: str) -> tuple[str, str]:
80:     match = re.search(r"合\s*计\s*¥?(-?[0-9]+(?:\.[0-9]+)?)\s+([*¥]?-?[0-9]+(?:\.[0-9]+)?|\*)", text)
81:     if not match:
82:         raise MissingFieldError("Missing required field: 合计/税额")
83:     amount_raw = match.group(1)
84:     tax_raw = match.group(2)
85:     if tax_raw == "*":
86:         tax_raw = "0"
87:     return amount_raw, tax_raw.replace("¥", "")
88: 
89: 
90: def _extract_total_amount(text: str) -> str:
91:     patterns = (
92:         r"价税合计.*?[（(]小写[)）]\s*¥?(-?[0-9]+(?:\.[0-9]+)?)",
93:         r"票价[:：]?\s*￥?(-?[0-9]+(?:\.[0-9]+)?)",
94:         r"￥(-?[0-9]+(?:\.[0-9]+)?)",
95:     )
96:     for pattern in patterns:
97:         match = re.search(pattern, text, re.MULTILINE | re.DOTALL)
98:         if match:
99:             return match.group(1)
100:     raise MissingFieldError("Missing required field: 价税合计")

(End of file - total 100 lines)

8:

10: def process_invoices(request: ProcessRequest) -> ProcessResult:
11:     if request.progress_callback:
12:         request.progress_callback("validating", 0, 0, "Resolving inputs...")
13:         
14:     resolved_input = resolve_input(request.input_path, request.output_path, request.overwrite)
15: 
16:     total_files = len(resolved_input.pdf_paths)
17:     if request.progress_callback:
18:         request.progress_callback("processing", 0, total_files, f"Found {total_files} files...")
19: 
20:     processed_count = 0
21:     failed_files: list[str] = []
22:     duplicate_skips = 0
23:     conflict_skips = 0
24:     conflicts: dict[str, str] = {}
25:     records_by_invoice_number: dict[str, object] = {}
26: 
27:     for pdf_path in resolved_input.pdf_paths:
28:         processed_count += 1
29:         if request.progress_callback:
30:             request.progress_callback("processing", processed_count, total_files, f"Processing {pdf_path.name}...")
31:         try:
32:             raw_text = read_pdf_text(pdf_path)
33:             record = extract_invoice_record(raw_text, pdf_path)
34:         except (InvoiceToolError, ValueError) as exc:
35:             failed_files.append(f"{pdf_path}: {exc}")
36:             continue
37: 
38:         existing = records_by_invoice_number.get(record.发票号码)
39:         if existing is None:
40:             records_by_invoice_number[record.发票号码] = record
41:             continue
42: 
43:         if existing == record:
44:             duplicate_skips += 1
45:             continue
46: 
47:         conflict_skips += 1
48:         conflicts[str(pdf_path)] = _build_conflict_summary(existing, record)
49: 
50:     records = list(records_by_invoice_number.values())
51:     if not records:
52:         raise NoSuccessfulInvoicesError("No invoices were successfully extracted")
53: 
54:     if request.progress_callback:
55:         request.progress_callback("exporting", processed_count, total_files, f"Sorting and exporting {len(records)} records...")
56: 
57:     records.sort(key=lambda item: (item.开票日期 == "", item.开票日期, item.发票号码))
58: 
59:     if request.progress_callback:
60:         request.progress_callback("complete", processed_count, total_files, "Done")
61: 
62:     return ProcessResult(
63:         processed_count=processed_count,
64:         exported_count=len(records),
65:         failed_files=failed_files,
66:         duplicate_skips=duplicate_skips,
67:         conflict_skips=conflict_skips,
68:         output_path=str(Path(request.output_path)),
69:         records=records,
70:         conflicts=conflicts,
71:     )
72: 
73: 
74: def _build_conflict_summary(existing_record, incoming_record) -> str:
75:     differing_fields: list[str] = []
76:     for field_name in (
77:         "文件名",
78:         "开票日期",
79:         "购买方名称",
80:         "购买方税号",

82:         "销售方税号",
83:         "金额",
84:         "税额",
85:         "价税合计",
86:     ):
87:         existing_value = getattr(existing_record, field_name)
88:         incoming_value = getattr(incoming_record, field_name)
89:         if existing_value != incoming_value:
90:             differing_fields.append(f"{field_name}: '{existing_value}' != '{incoming_value}'")
91:     joined_fields = "; ".join(differing_fields) if differing_fields else "no differing fields captured"
92:     return f"invoice={incoming_record.发票号码}; {joined_fields}"

Read-only external/library guidance: for Python openpyxl/pandas workflows, find the cleanest way to apply a background fill to rows in an exported workbook based on record completeness. Focus on post-export styling patterns that preserve fixed column order and are compatible with pandas-generated xlsx files. Return concise best practices only. Do not modify files.
<!-- OMO_INTERNAL_INITIATOR -->

[assistant (librarian)] 2026-03-19T01:50:32.346Z
This is a **TYPE A: CONCEPTUAL** question. Let me do a quick documentation check, then give you concise best practices.

[assistant (librarian)] 2026-03-19T01:50:46.030Z
## Best Practices: Row Background Fill Based on Record Completeness

### 1. **Post-Export Pattern (Load → Style → Save)**

```python
import pandas as pd
from openpyxl import load_workbook
from openpyxl.styles import PatternFill

# Step 1: Export with fixed column order (usecols preserves order)
df.to_excel('output.xlsx', index=False, sheet_name='Data', 
            columns=['id', 'name', 'status', 'date'])  # explicit col order

# Step 2: Post-export styling (openpyxl loads what's already there)
wb = load_workbook('output.xlsx')
ws = wb.active

complete_fill = PatternFill(start_color='C6EFCE', end_color='C6EFCE', fill_type='solid')
incomplete_fill = PatternFill(start_color='FFC7CE', end_color='FFC7CE', fill_type='solid')

# Determine completeness — use a status/reference column
for row in ws.iter_rows(min_row=2, max_row=ws.max_row):
    status_cell = row[2]  # e.g., "status" column (0-indexed after id,name)
    if status_cell.value == 'complete':
        for cell in row:
            cell.fill = complete_fill
    else:
        for cell in row:
            cell.fill = incomplete_fill

wb.save('output.xlsx')
```

### 2. **Two Complementary Approaches**

| Approach | When to Use | Key API |
|---|---|---|
| **Iterate rows + set cell fills** | Simple categorical completeness (complete/incomplete) | `ws.iter_rows()`, `cell.fill = PatternFill(...)` |
| **Conditional Formatting** | Dynamic, Excel-native rules (survives re-save in Excel) | `ws.conditional_formatting.add()`, `FormulaRule` |

### 3. **Conditional Formatting for Row-Level Rules (Recommended)**

```python
from openpyxl.formatting.rule import FormulaRule

# Range must span all columns; formula anchors to trigger column
# $C = status column (locked letter, free row)
ws.conditional_formatting.add(
    f'A2:{ws.max_column}{ws.max_row}',
    FormulaRule(
        formula=['$C2="complete"'],   # locked column C, row follows
        fill=PatternFill(start_color='C6EFCE', fill_type='solid')
    )
)
ws.conditional_formatting.add(
    f'A2:{ws.max_column}{ws.max_row}',
    FormulaRule(
        formula=['$C2="incomplete"'],
        fill=PatternFill(start_color='FFC7CE', fill_type='solid')
    )
)
```

### 4. **Completeness Heuristic (Row-Level)**

```python
# Count non-null values per row vs expected column count
expected_cols = len(df.columns)  # use original df column count
for row in ws.iter_rows(min_row=2, max_row=ws.max_row):
    filled = sum(1 for cell in row if cell.value is not None)
    pct = filled / expected_cols
    if pct >= 1.0:
        fill = complete_fill
    elif pct >= 0.5:
        fill = partial_fill
    else:
        fill = incomplete_fill
    for cell in row:
        cell.fill = fill
```

### 5. **Key Guardrails**

- **Fixed column order**: Pass explicit `columns=` list to `to_excel()` so positions are predictable for post-export indexing.
- **No `values_only=True`**: When iterating to apply fills, omit `values_only=True` — you need the `Cell` objects to set `.fill`.
- **`fill_type="solid"`**: Required; without it, the fill won't render in Excel.
- **6-char hex without `#`**: Use `'FFC7CE'` not `'#FFC7CE'` for `start_color`.
- **Anchor the column, not the row** in conditional formatting formulas: `$C2` (column locked) not `C$2`.
- **Apply fills to all cells in the row**: Either loop each cell, or use `ws[f"{row}"]` row slicer syntax — single-cell fill on one column does NOT auto-propagate.
```

<answer>
## Current Data Flow (Read-Only Analysis)

The pipeline flows: **CLI/GUI → service.py process_invoices() → extractor.py extract_invoice_record() → pdf/reader.py → excel/exporter.py export_records_to_excel()**

### Where Partial Invoices Are Currently Dropped

**Root cause: `D:\test\jiali\code\invoice_tool\application\extractor.py`**

Every extraction step uses `_require_match()` (lines 14–15, 37–41), which raises `MissingFieldError` on the **first** missing field, skipping all remaining fields. The caller in `service.py` catches this (lines 34–36) and adds the file to `failed_files`, then `continue`s — the record is silently discarded. No distinction is made between a truly unreadable PDF and a PDF that was only partially parseable.

The sort key on `service.py` line 57 (`item.开票日期 == ""`) already sorts invoices with empty dates to the end — this is the exact mechanism needed for partial records. Currently this only catches cases where `开票日期` regex fails; it doesn't handle records with multiple missing fields.

---

## Minimum Code Changes (4 Files, Targeted Edits)

### Change 1 — `D:\test\jiali\code\invoice_tool\application\extractor.py`
**Goal: Return partial records instead of raising on first missing field.**

Add a new helper that returns `None` instead of raising, and refactor each field extractor to be non-fatal:

| Line | Change |
|------|--------|
| 37–41 | Replace `_require_match()` with `_try_match()` that returns `match.group(1).strip() if match else ""`. Each call site at lines 14, 15, 17–21 uses `_try_match` instead. |
| 44–57 | Refactor `_extract_counterparty_names()` to return `(buyer_or_empty, seller_or_empty)` instead of raising `MissingFieldError`. |
| 66–76 | Refactor `_extract_counterparty_tax_ids()` to return `(buyer_tax_or_empty, seller_tax_or_empty)`. |
| 79–87 | Refactor `_extract_totals()` to return `(amount_or_empty, tax_or_empty)`. |
| 90–100 | Refactor `_extract_total_amount()` to return `total_or_empty`. |

`extract_invoice_record()` at lines 9–34 becomes non-throwing: it fills missing fields with `""` (empty string) and always returns an `InvoiceRecord`. Any PDF that crashes earlier (PDF unreadable, zero text) still raises `UnreadablePDFError` — those are genuinely failed files, not partial invoices.

---

### Change 2 — `D:\test\jiali\code\invoice_tool\application\service.py`
**Goal: Distinguish partial vs. complete records; keep partials in the export list.**

| Line | Change |
|------|--------|
| 21 | Add `partial_records: list[InvoiceRecord] = []` alongside `failed_files`. |
| 34–36 | After catching `InvoiceToolError`/`ValueError`, check if the error is specifically `MissingFieldError`. If so, retry extraction with the new non-throwing fallback method, append to `partial_records`, and `continue`. Other errors (PDF unreadable) still go to `failed_files`. |
| 50 | Build `complete_records` (all 10 fields non-empty) and `partial_records` by checking each record's fields. Alternatively, track during extraction. |
| 52 | Remove the all-or-nothing `NoSuccessfulInvoicesError` check or relax it to "no complete and no partial records". |
| 57 | Update sort: `complete_records` sorted by `(开票日期, 发票号码)`; `partial_records` appended after complete ones (same sort key so both groups are internally sorted). |
| 62–70 | Add `partial_count=len(partial_records)` to `ProcessResult` and include `partial_records` in the result. |
| 74–91 | `_build_conflict_summary` unchanged. |

**Alternative minimal approach (fewer changes):** Instead of a separate `partial_records` list, add a boolean flag `_is_partial` to `InvoiceRecord` in the domain model. Refill missing fields with `""` for all records. Then in `service.py` just filter `records` into complete-first and partial-last groups for sorting.

---

### Change 3 — `D:\test\jiali\code\invoice_tool\infrastructure\excel\exporter.py`
**Goal: Apply a yellow fill (`FFFF00`) to rows with any empty field.**

| Line | Change |
|------|--------|
| 1 | Add `from openpyxl.styles import PatternFill, Font` |
| 22–26 | Refactor `export_records_to_excel()` to accept two lists: `complete_records` and `partial_records`. Build one combined list `all_records = complete_records + partial_records`. Create DataFrame from `all_records`. |
| After `dataframe.to_excel(...)` | Open the saved workbook with `openpyxl`, iterate rows starting at row 2 (row 1 = header), check `row[col].value == ""` for any cell. If any cell is empty, apply `PatternFill(fill_type="solid", fgColor="FFFF00")` to the entire row. Save and close. |

| 30 | Add `partial_records: List[InvoiceRecord] = field(default_factory=list)` |

### Downstream Adapters (2 Files — Print/Display Updates Only)

| File | Change |
|------|--------|
| `D:\test\jiali\code\invoice_tool\cli\main.py` lines 24–43 | Pass `partial_records` to exporter: `export_records_to_excel(result.records + result.partial_records, ...)`. Add `print(f"partial={result.partial_count}")`. |
| `D:\test\jiali\code\invoice_tool\gui\controller.py` line 153 | Same `export_records_to_excel(result.records + result.partial_records, ...)` pass-through. In `SummaryMetrics` add `partial: int = 0` and map `result.partial_count`. In `map_process_result_to_gui_data()` include partial in summary. |
| `D:\test\jiali\code\invoice_tool\gui\app.py` lines 460–466 | Add a sixth metric tile `("⚡", "部分提取", "partial", "#fff8e1", "#a16207", "#ca8a04")` with the amber/yellow palette matching the Excel highlight. Optionally add a "partial details" tab showing which fields were blank per record. |

---

## Key Design Decisions

- **`""` as sentinel for missing fields**: Already consistent with current sort key logic (`item.开票日期 == ""`). No schema change needed in `InvoiceRecord`.
- **Partial rows highlighted yellow (`FFFF00`)**: Contrasts cleanly with the white background and is semantically consistent across Excel, GUI (amber metric tile), and CLI (`partial=` counter).
- **Partial records sorted to the end**: Uses the existing sort infrastructure — partial records (with `""` in at least one field) naturally fall after complete records when sorted by `(field == "", field, ...)`.
- **Unreadable PDFs (`UnreadablePDFError`) stay in `failed_files`**: These are genuinely broken files, not partial invoices. No behavior change for that category.
</answer>

<next_steps>
All 7 files above are identified with their specific line-change targets. The implementation is additive: partial records are extracted alongside complete ones, sorted to the end via existing sort logic, and styled in Excel with openpyxl. No existing behavior (complete-invoice export, failed-file handling, duplicate/conflict logic) needs to be broken. The changes are ready to proceed.
</next_steps>

<content>1: # PDF Invoice to Excel aggregation tool
2: 
3: A tool to extract invoice data from text-based PDF invoices and aggregate them into an Excel spreadsheet.
4: 
5: ## Installation
6: 
7: 1. Ensure you have Python 3.8+ installed.
8: 2. Clone this repository.
9: 3. Install dependencies:
10:    ```bash
11:    pip install -r requirements.txt
12:    ```
13: 
14: ## Usage
15: 
16: The tool provides both a Command-Line Interface (CLI) and a Graphical User Interface (GUI).
17: 
18: ### Graphical User Interface (GUI)
19: 
20: Launch the GUI using:
21: 
22: ```bash
23: python -m invoice_tool.gui
24: ```
25: 
26: **Features:**
27: - **Drag and Drop**: Drop a single PDF file or a folder containing PDFs onto the input area.
28: - **One-Item Limit**: The GUI supports dropping only one item (file or folder) at a time.
29: - **Progress Tracking**: Real-time progress bar and status updates during processing.
30: - **Results Summary**: Visual summary of processed, exported, failed, and duplicate records.
31: - **Detailed Logs**: View failed files and duplicate conflict details within the app.
32: 
33: **V1 Limitations:**
34: - No "Cancel" button once processing starts.
35: - No history of previous runs.
36: - Not packaged as a standalone installer (requires Python environment).
37: 
38: ### Command-Line Interface (CLI)
39: 
40: Run the CLI using the following command:
41: 
42: ```bash
43: python -m invoice_tool.cli --input <input_path> --output <output_path> [--overwrite]
44: ```
45: 
46: #### Examples

51: python -m invoice_tool.cli --input "D:\test\jiali\invoice\三亚京东佳禹贸易有限公司-发票金额29.pdf" --output "D:\test\jiali\code\out\single.xlsx" --overwrite
52: ```

63: - `--overwrite`: (Optional) Overwrite the output file if it already exists.

72: 3. Run the folder command above and confirm a batch workbook is created under `out\batch.xlsx`.
73: 4. Re-run the folder command without `--overwrite` against the same output path and confirm the command exits with an overwrite error.
74: 5. Confirm the CLI prints any failed-file entries and duplicate-conflict details when they occur during folder processing.
75: 
76: ### GUI Verification

81: 4. Try dragging multiple files. Confirm an error message appears and the input is rejected.
82: 5. Select an output path under the `out\` directory and click "START PROCESSING".
83: 6. Confirm the progress bar completes and a success message appears.
84: 7. Verify the output Excel file in the `out\` folder contains the expected data.
85:

94: class Controller:
95:     def __init__(self, root):
96:         self.root = root
97:         self.state = GuiState()
98:         self.event_queue = queue.Queue()
99:         self._worker_thread: Optional[threading.Thread] = None
100: 
101:     def set_input(self, path_str: str) -> Tuple[bool, str]:
102:         """Validates and sets the input path in the state."""
103:         if not path_str:
104:             self.state.input_path = ""
105:             self.state.input_mode = InputMode.NONE
106:             return False, "未提供路径。"
107: 
108:         path = Path(path_str)
109:         if not path.exists():
110:             return False, f"路径不存在：{path_str}"
111: 
112:         if path.is_file():
113:             if path.suffix.lower() != ".pdf":
114:                 return False, "文件不是 PDF。"
115:             self.state.input_path = str(path.absolute())
116:             self.state.input_mode = InputMode.FILE
117:             return True, "已选择有效 PDF 文件。"
118:         
119:         if path.is_dir():
120:             # In V1 GUI, we allow selecting any directory. 
121:             # If it has no PDFs, the backend will surface an error during processing.
122:             self.state.input_path = str(path.absolute())
123:             self.state.input_mode = InputMode.FOLDER
124:             pdf_files = list(path.glob("*.pdf"))
125:             return True, f"已选择文件夹（共 {len(pdf_files)} 个 PDF）。"
126: 
127:         return False, "输入类型无效。"
128: 
129:     def set_output(self, path_str: str) -> Tuple[bool, str]:
130:         """Sets the output path in the state."""
131:         if not path_str:
132:             return False, "未提供路径。"
133:         self.state.output_path = path_str
134:         return True, "输出路径已设置。"
135: 
136:     def run_pipeline_sync(self, progress_callback: Optional[Callable[[ProgressEvent], None]] = None) -> ProcessResult:
137:         """
138:         GUI-safe backend adapter running the existing processing pipeline.
139:         Currently blocking (sync) but designed so a background worker thread can just 
140:         wrap this call.
141:         """
142:         def _service_callback(phase: str, completed: int, total: int, message: str) -> None:
143:             if progress_callback:
144:                 progress_callback(ProgressEvent(phase, completed, total, message))
145: 
146:         req = ProcessRequest(
147:             input_path=self.state.input_path,
148:             output_path=self.state.output_path,
149:             overwrite=self.state.overwrite,
150:             progress_callback=_service_callback
151:         )
152:         result = process_invoices(req)
153:         export_records_to_excel(result.records, self.state.output_path)
154:         return result
155: 
156:     def start_processing(self):
157:         """Starts the processing pipeline in a background thread."""
158:         if self._worker_thread and self._worker_thread.is_alive():
159:             return
160: 
161:         self._worker_thread = threading.Thread(target=self._run_worker, daemon=True)
162:         self._worker_thread.start()
163: 
164:     def _run_worker(self):
165:         """Worker thread target."""
166:         try:
167:             def _progress_callback(event: ProgressEvent):
168:                 self.event_queue.put(("progress", event))
169: 
170:             result = self.run_pipeline_sync(progress_callback=_progress_callback)
171:             self.event_queue.put(("result", result))
172:         except Exception as e:
173:             # Wrap error in ProgressEvent for explicit phase semantics
174:             self.event_queue.put(("error", ProgressEvent(
175:                 phase="error", 
176:                 completed=0, 
177:                 total=0, 
178:                 message=str(e)
179:             )))

186:     def _on_drop(self, event):
187:         if self.controller.state.phase == AppPhase.PROCESSING:
188:             return
189:         # tkinterdnd2 can return multiple files as a brace-delimited string
190:         # if they contain spaces. On Windows, backslashes might be doubled or escaped.
191:         # We use a regex to correctly split the tcl list string.
192:         data = event.data
193:         
194:         # Tcl list splitting: matches items inside {braces} or items without spaces
195:         files = re.findall(r'\{(.*?)\}|([^\s{}]+)', data)
196:         # findall with multiple groups returns a list of tuples, flatten and filter empty
197:         files = [item[0] if item[0] else item[1] for item in files]
198:         
199:         if len(files) > 1:
200:             self._set_status("错误：一次仅支持拖放 1 个文件或文件夹。", "error")
201:             return
202: 
203:         path = files[0]
204:         self._update_input_from_path(path)

310:     def _set_ui_state(self, phase: AppPhase):

327:     def _poll_queue(self):
328:         try:
329:             while True:
330:                 msg_type, data = self.controller.event_queue.get_nowait()
331:                 if msg_type == "progress":
332:                     self._handle_progress(data)
333:                 elif msg_type == "result":
334:                     self._handle_result(data)
335:                     return # Stop polling
336:                 elif msg_type == "error":
337:                     self._handle_error(data)
338:                     return # Stop polling
339:         except tk.TclError:
340:             # Handle case where widget is destroyed during poll
341:             return
342:         except Exception:
343:             # No message in queue
344:             pass
345:         
346:         # Continue polling if not done
347:         if self.controller.state.phase == AppPhase.PROCESSING:
348:             self.after(100, self._poll_queue)
349: 
350:     def _handle_progress(self, event):
351:         self._set_status(_localize_phase_message(event.phase, event.message), event.phase)
352:         
353:         # Phase-based progress semantics: indeterminate for preflight/setup, determinate for processing
354:         if event.phase in ("validating", "exporting"):
355:             if self.progress_bar['mode'] != 'indeterminate':
356:                 self.progress_bar.configure(mode='indeterminate')
357:                 self.progress_bar.start(10)
358:         else:
359:             if self.progress_bar['mode'] != 'determinate':
360:                 self.progress_bar.stop()

569: def _extract_filename_from_message(message: str) -> str:
570:     if not message:

573:     if m:

578: def _localize_phase_message(phase: str, raw_message: str) -> str:
579:     if phase == "validating":
580:         return "正在校验输入..."
581:     if phase == "processing":
582:         file_name = _extract_filename_from_message(raw_message)
583:         return f"正在处理：{file_name}" if file_name else "正在处理发票..."
584:     if phase == "exporting":
585:         return "正在导出 Excel..."
586:     if phase == "complete":
587:         return "处理完成。"
588:     if phase == "error":
589:         return f"错误：{raw_message}" if raw_message else "处理失败。"

145: 
146:         req = ProcessRequest(
147:             input_path=self.state.input_path,
148:             output_path=self.state.output_path,
149:             overwrite=self.state.overwrite,
150:             progress_callback=_service_callback
151:         )
152:         result = process_invoices(req)
153:         export_records_to_excel(result.records, self.state.output_path)
154:         return result
155: 
156:     def start_processing(self):
157:         """Starts the processing pipeline in a background thread."""
158:         if self._worker_thread and self._worker_thread.is_alive():
159:             return
160: 
161:         self._worker_thread = threading.Thread(target=self._run_worker, daemon=True)
162:         self._worker_thread.start()
163: 
164:     def _run_worker(self):
165:         """Worker thread target."""
166:         try:
167:             def _progress_callback(event: ProgressEvent):
168:                 self.event_queue.put(("progress", event))
169: 
170:             result = self.run_pipeline_sync(progress_callback=_progress_callback)
171:             self.event_queue.put(("result", result))
172:         except Exception as e:
173:             # Wrap error in ProgressEvent for explicit phase semantics
174:             self.event_queue.put(("error", ProgressEvent(
175:                 phase="error", 
176:                 completed=0, 
177:                 total=0, 
178:                 message=str(e)
179:             )))

(End of file - total 179 lines)
</content>
```
